21:507:39782:55:28:71:274:626:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f3:C:IV. Data and Institutional Background 
21:508:39819:28:28:107:512:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Elementary students in Chicago public schools take a standardized, multiple-choice 
21:509:39902:28:27:71:511:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:achievement exam known as the Iowa Test of Basic Skills (ITBS).  The ITBS is a national, 
21:510:39991:27:28:71:541:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:norm-referenced exam with a reading comprehension section and three separate math sections.13  
21:511:40086:28:27:71:531:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Third through eighth grade students in Chicago are required to take the exams each year.  Most 
21:512:40181:27:28:71:521:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:schools administer the exams to first and second grade students as well, although this is not a 
21:513:40277:28:27:71:157:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:district mandate.  
21:514:40296:27:28:107:535:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Our base sample includes all students in third to seventh grade for the years 1993.14  For 
21:515:40387:28:28:71:509:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:each student, we have the question-by-question answer string on each year’s ITBS reading 
21:516:40476:28:27:71:533:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:comprehension and mathematics tests, school and classroom identifiers, the full history of prior 
21:517:40573:27:28:71:503:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and future test scores, and demographic variables including age, sex, race, and free lunch 
21:518:40664:28:27:71:509:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:eligibility. We also have information about school-level characteristics including mobility, 
21:519:40757:27:28:71:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:poverty and attendance rates, racial composition and average teacher characteristics including 
21:520:40852:28:28:71:500:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent with an MA+ degree, years of experience, and undergraduate major.  We do not, 
21:521:40938:28:27:71:500:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:however, have individual teacher identifiers, so we are unable to directly link teachers to 
21:522:41030:27:35:71:327:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms or to track a particular teacher over time. 
21:523:41085:35:7:215:218:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
21:524:41143:42:16:71:497:170:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:13 There are also other parts of the test which are either not included in official school reporting (spelling, 
21:525:41255:16:11:71:520:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:punctuation, grammar) or are given only in select grades (science and social studies), for which we do not have 
21:526:41367:11:7:71:123:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:information. 
21:527:41380:7:16:71:542:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:14  We exclude eighth graders because our algorithm requires test score data for the following year and the ITBS test 
21:528:41498:16:12:71:540:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:is not administered to ninth graders.  Another standardized test is given to ninth graders, but a substantial fraction of 
21:529:41620:12:0:71:435:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:the students fail to take that test and it is not directly comparable to the elementary exams. 
22:530:41717:0:27:107:536:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Because our cheating proxies rely on comparisons to past and future test scores, we drop 
22:531:41806:27:28:71:541:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:observations that are missing reading or math scores in either the preceding year or the following 
22:532:41905:28:27:71:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:year.15  Students with missing demographic data are also excluded from the analysis.  Finally, 
22:533:42000:27:28:71:531:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:because our algorithms for identifying cheating rely on identifying suspicious patterns within a 
22:534:42097:28:28:71:500:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classroom, our methods have little power in classrooms with small numbers of students.  
22:535:42185:28:27:71:510:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Consequently, we drop all classrooms for which we have fewer than ten valid students in a 
22:536:42275:27:28:71:510:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:particular grade after our other exclusions.  A handful of classrooms with impossibly large 
22:537:42367:28:27:71:542:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:number of students – presumably multiple classrooms combined into one – are also dropped. Our 
22:538:42461:27:28:71:475:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:final data set contains roughly 20,000 students per grade per year distributed across 
22:539:42547:28:27:71:524:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:approximately 1,000 classrooms, for a total of over 40,000 classroom-years of data (with four 
22:540:42641:27:28:71:447:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subject tests per classroom-year) and over 700,000 student-year observations. 
22:541:42719:28:28:107:518:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Summary statistics for the full sample of classrooms are shown in the first column of 
22:542:42805:28:27:71:505:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Table 1, with the unit of observation being at the level of class*subject*year.  The second 
22:543:42897:27:28:71:505:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:column of Table 1 reports student-level summary statistics for the subset of our sample of 
22:544:42988:28:27:71:528:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms we classify as likely to have cheated.  Classrooms we suspect of cheating are more 
22:545:43082:27:28:71:464:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:likely to be subject to the accountability policies and students in these classes are 
22:546:43168:28:28:71:539:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:disproportionately from the bottom half of the achievement.  School-level teacher characteristics 
22:547:43266:28:27:71:427:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:do not differ much between the whole sample and the suspected cheaters. 
22:548:43338:27:28:107:523:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The ITBS exams are administered over a week long period in early May.  Third grade 
22:549:43421:28:27:71:533:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:teachers are permitted to administer the exam to their own students, while other teachers switch 
22:550:43518:27:26:71:522:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classes to administer the exams.  The exams are generally delivered to the schools one to two 
22:551:43612:26:7:215:218:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
22:552:43670:33:0:71:524:124:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:15  Test data may be missing either because a student did not attend school on the days of the test, or because the 
23:553:43788:0:27:71:517:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:weeks before testing, and are supposed to be kept in a secure location by the principal or the 
23:554:43883:27:28:71:539:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:school’s test coordinator, an individual in the school designated to coordinate the testing process 
23:555:43983:28:27:71:509:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(often a counselor or administrator).  Each section of the exam consist of 30 to 60 multiple 
23:556:44076:27:28:71:531:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:choice questions which students are given between 30 and 75 minutes to complete.16   Students 
23:557:44170:28:28:71:505:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:mark their responses on answer sheets, which are scanned to determine a student’s score.  
23:558:44260:28:27:71:528:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Teachers or administrators then “clean” the answer keys, erasing stray pencil marks, removing 
23:559:44354:27:28:71:532:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dirt or debris from the form, and darkening item responses that were only faintly marked by the 
23:560:44450:28:27:71:508:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:student.  At the end of the week, the test coordinators at each school deliver the completed 
23:561:44543:27:28:71:523:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:answer keys and exams to the CPS central office.  School personnel are not permitted to keep 
23:562:44636:28:27:71:541:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:copies of the actual exams, although school officials acknowledge that a number of teachers each 
23:563:44733:27:28:71:524:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:year do so.  The CPS has administered three different versions of the ITBS between 1993 and 
23:564:44825:28:28:71:521:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:C:2000.  The CPS alternates forms each year, with new forms being offered for the first time in 
23:565:44919:28:27:71:208:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1993, 1994 and 1997.17        
23:566:44949:27:28:107:532:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The exams are scored electronically by CPS central office staff.  There is no penalty for 
23:567:45039:28:27:71:542:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:guessing, so that a student’s raw score is simply calculated as the sum of correct responses on the 
23:568:45139:27:28:71:514:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:exam.  The raw score is then translated into a metric known as grade equivalents, which are 
23:569:45231:28:55:71:517:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:normed so that a student at the 50th percentile in the nation scores at the eighth month of her 
23:570:45327:55:12:539:542:212:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                                                                                                                                                           
23:571:45513:67:7:71:509:200:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:student transferred into the CPS system in the current year or left the system prior to the next year of testing. 
23:572:45627:7:16:71:523:193:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:16The mathematics and reading tests measure basic skills.  The reading comprehension exam consists of three to 
23:573:45738:16:11:71:539:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:eight short passages followed by up to nine questions relating to the passage.  The passages include poetry, fictional 
23:574:45857:11:12:71:533:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:stories, and narratives on historical, scientific or literary topics.  The questions assess factual recall (e.g., Who was 
23:575:45979:12:11:71:516:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:the main character in the story?) as well as critical analysis (e.g., What was the main idea of the passage?) and 
23:576:46093:11:12:71:532:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:interpretation (e.g., How do you think Jose felt at the end of the story?).  The math exam consists of three sections 
23:577:46211:12:7:71:330:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:that assess number concepts, problem-solving and computation. 
23:578:46273:7:16:71:533:124:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:17 These three forms are used for re-testing, summer school testing, and mid-year testing as well, so that it is likely 
23:579:46393:16:0:71:399:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:that over the years, teachers have seen the same exam on a number of occasions.  
24:580:46476:0:27:71:530:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:current grade.  For example, an average third grader taking the test in the eighth month of third 
24:581:46574:27:28:71:536:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:grade will score a 3.8.  Similarly, a sixth grader that scores a 5.8 is one year behind grade level.  
24:582:46676:28:27:107:110:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: 
24:583:46676:55:28:71:285:626:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:V. Estimating the Prevalence of Cheating 
24:584:46717:28:28:107:515:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:We undertake a determination of the prevalence of cheating in three steps.  First, we 
24:585:46803:28:27:71:530:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:analyze whether our cheating measures are actually effective at detecting cheating.  To do this, 
24:586:46900:27:28:71:542:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:we artificially alter student answers in ways that might mimic teacher cheating and then see if we 
24:587:46999:28:27:71:519:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:catch the classrooms for which we ourselves have cheated.  In addition, we also alter student 
24:588:47093:27:28:71:514:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:answers in a way that may reflect a class that has large, legitimate test score gains due to an 
24:589:47189:28:27:71:537:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:outstanding teacher, demonstrating that our measures are much less likely to mistakenly classify 
24:590:47286:27:28:71:537:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:such gains as cheating.  Second, we examine the empirical distribution of our cheating measures 
24:591:47382:28:28:71:533:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in the portion of the sample unlikely to be heavily contaminated by cheating.  This provides the 
24:592:47479:28:27:71:533:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:basis for constructing a non-cheating counterfactual against which the actual data is compared.  
24:593:47576:27:28:71:462:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, we present the basic findings with respect to the estimated cheating rate. 
24:594:47660:28:27:71:74:322:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:!: 
24:595:47660:55:28:71:393:295:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:a) Do the cheating measures actually detect cheating classrooms? 
24:596:47725:28:28:107:507:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Because we do not know which classrooms are cheating, we have no direct way of 
24:597:47804:28:27:71:502:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:knowing whether our measures actually detect cheating.  One indirect way of testing this 
24:598:47893:27:28:71:537:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:hypothesis, however, is to simulate cheating and then ascertain whether our measures detect this 
24:599:47990:28:27:71:537:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:artificial cheating.  In this section, we simulate two different types of teacher cheating.  The first 
24:600:48093:27:28:71:527:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is a very naive version, in which a teacher starts cheating at the same question for a number of 
24:601:48190:28:0:71:521:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students and changes consecutive questions to the right answers for these students, creating a 
25:602:48287:0:27:71:477:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:block of identical and correct responses.  The second type of cheating is much more 
25:603:48371:27:28:71:528:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sophisticated: we randomly change answers from incorrect to correct for selected students in a 
25:604:48466:28:27:71:510:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:class.18  For the purposes of comparison, we also present results attempting to simulate the 
25:605:48559:27:28:71:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:effects of a good teacher inducing the same gain among students in the class.  The impact of a 
25:606:48654:28:28:71:508:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:good teacher will differ in two ways from a cheating teacher: (1) some of the gains will be 
25:607:48746:28:27:71:521:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:preserved in the following year, and (2) the students will not get random answers correct, but 
25:608:48841:27:28:71:540:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rather, will tend to show the greatest improvement on the easiest questions that the students were 
25:609:48940:28:27:71:520:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:getting wrong.  For both types of cheating and the good teacher scenario, we run simulations 
25:610:49033:27:28:71:537:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:changing 3, 6 or 9 questions for 25, 50 or 100 percent of the students in the classroom.  We alter 
25:611:49132:28:27:71:538:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the answer strings for every classroom, one classroom at a time, tallying the fraction of the cases 
25:612:49232:27:28:71:525:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in which the artificially cheating classroom exceeds our strictest threshold (95th percentile) on 
25:613:49330:28:28:71:527:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:both ANSWERS and SCORE.  We present the results for 5th grade reading in 1993.  This grade 
25:614:49421:28:27:71:541:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and year was selected because we want our baseline sample to be as free of cheating as possible.  
25:615:49519:27:28:71:543:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:In theory, the incentives for teachers to cheat in that grade and year are low because this is before 
25:616:49621:28:27:71:522:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:accountability reforms and fifth-grade test outcomes were not widely publicized at that time.  
25:617:49716:27:28:107:534:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Table 2 reports the results of the simulation.  As a point of reference, 1.13 percent of the 
25:618:49809:28:28:71:530:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms in the actual data exceed the thresholds we use in the table for labeling a classroom 
25:619:49906:28:27:71:524:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:as cheating.  For the most minor case of cheating (3 questions for 25 percent of the class), our 
25:620:50003:27:28:71:515:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating indicator picks up less than 4 and 2 percent respectively of the unsophisticated and 
25:621:50097:28:27:71:521:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sophisticated cheating. The good teacher is no more likely to be labeled a cheater in this case 
25:622:50193:27:26:71:518:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:than is a randomly drawn classroom in the actual data.  As the extent of cheating increases – 
25:623:50287:26:7:215:218:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
25:624:50345:33:0:71:541:124:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:18  We have also experimented with forms of cheating with intermediate degrees of sophistication.  Not surprisingly, 
26:625:50464:0:27:71:528:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:either by increasing the number of students or the number of questions altered – the success of 
26:626:50560:27:28:71:539:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the algorithm improves greatly, but it is still far from perfect.  If six questions are altered for half 
26:627:50665:28:27:71:538:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the class, more than 50 percent of the unsophisticated cheaters are detected, as well as more than 
26:628:50764:27:28:71:538:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:one-third of the sophisticated cheaters.  The likelihood that a good teacher is labeled as a cheater 
26:629:50865:28:28:71:531:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is still less than 3 percent.  By the most extreme cases we examine (9 questions for 100 percent 
26:630:50962:28:27:71:522:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of the class), roughly 90 percent of classrooms are categorized as cheating.  In the case, good 
26:631:51058:27:28:71:532:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:teachers will be identified as cheating nearly 40 percent of the time as well.  Thus, to the extent 
26:632:51158:28:27:71:531:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that there are teachers capable of such remarkable feats (it implies that the mean test score gain 
26:633:51257:27:28:71:533:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in the classroom in one year is well over two grade-equivalents, something observed in roughly 
26:634:51352:28:27:71:506:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:one in 1,000 classrooms in our sample, even with cheaters included), there is a substantial 
26:635:51444:27:28:71:343:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:likelihood we will mistakenly label them as cheaters.19   
26:636:51502:28:28:107:534:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:In summary, our cheating indicators are quite effective at detecting extreme instances of 
26:637:51592:28:27:71:519:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating, even if done in a sophisticated manner by the teacher.  Many more limited cases of 
26:638:51685:27:28:71:515:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating will not be detected by our measures, particularly if the cheating is done cleverly.   
26:639:51781:28:27:71:505:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Thus, to the extent that actual cheating done by teachers is moderate in degree and/or of a 
26:640:51873:27:28:71:491:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sophisticated kind, many cheaters will slip through the cracks, and our estimates of the 
26:641:51962:28:28:71:538:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:prevalence of cheating classrooms are likely to be (perhaps very loose) lower bounds on the true 
26:642:52059:28:27:71:518:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:values. On the other hand, our algorithm does yield some false positives, which works in the 
26:643:52152:27:35:71:164:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:opposite direction. 
26:644:52172:35:11:539:542:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                                                                                                                                                           
26:645:52358:46:12:71:541:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:the effectiveness of our measures in detecting moderately sophisticated types of cheating falls in between our ability 
26:646:52477:12:7:71:282:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:to detect cheating in the two polar cases we present. 
26:647:52531:7:16:71:540:147:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:19  To the extent this is a major concern (e.g., if these results were going to be used in disciplinary actions), there are 
26:648:52655:16:11:71:521:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:alternative measures that could be employed which are less likely to catch actual cheaters, but also dramatically 
26:649:52769:11:12:71:519:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:reduce the likelihood that a good teacher would falsely be accused of cheating.  One such measure would be to 
26:650:52879:12:0:71:383:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:require that most or all of the current year’s gain is lost in the following year. 
27:651:52964:0:27:71:74:708:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:!: 
27:652:52964:27:28:71:518:681:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:b) Projecting the distribution of the cheating measures in a counterfactual with no cheating  
27:653:53058:28:27:107:533:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:If we knew with certainty the classrooms that were cheating, then the distribution of our 
27:654:53148:27:28:71:515:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating measures in non-cheating classrooms would be directly observable.20  Our sample, 
27:655:53238:28:28:71:503:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:however, is made up of an unknown mixture of cheating and non-cheating classes.  Since 
27:656:53325:28:27:71:528:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating classrooms are likely to have large test score fluctuations and unusual answer strings, 
27:657:53422:27:28:71:517:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:they are likely to be concentrated in the upper tails, leaving the remainder of the distribution 
27:658:53519:28:27:71:536:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:relatively free of cheating. By observing patterns in that portion of the distribution, it is possible 
27:659:53622:27:28:71:509:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to make reasonable predictions as to what the upper tail might look like absent cheating. 21 
27:660:53714:28:27:107:533:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: The top panel of Table 3 presents breakdowns of the fraction of cases in which SCORE 
27:661:53799:27:28:71:531:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is above each of our cutoffs, as a function of the quartile that ANSWERS falls into, omitting the 
27:662:53897:28:28:71:541:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:top quartile of ANSWERS because that is where the cheating classrooms are likely to be.  Among 
27:663:53992:28:27:71:526:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms with ANSWERS are in the 0-25th percentile (i.e. not suspicious at all), 16.3 percent 
27:664:54088:27:28:71:534:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have test score gains above the 80th percentile, 6.2 percent are above the 90th percentile, and 2.3 
27:665:54188:28:27:71:530:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent are above the 95th percentile.  As one moves to the right in the table, the answer strings 
27:666:54287:27:28:71:539:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:are becoming more suspicious.  The frequency of high values of SCORE rises slightly moving to 
27:667:54381:28:32:71:517:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the right, but the relationship is weak.  This mirrors the pattern presented earlier in Figure 1. 
27:668:54479:32:7:215:218:235:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
27:669:54537:39:16:71:529:228:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:20Of course, if we knew which classrooms were cheating, then this assumption would not be necessary in the first 
27:670:54650:16:7:71:97:212:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:place. 
27:671:54657:7:16:71:538:205:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:21 There are two potential biases at work in this sort of analysis.  First, some cheating classrooms are likely to evade 
27:672:54778:16:12:71:522:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:our measures and slip into the sample we are describing as non-cheaters.  Cheating classrooms will probably be 
27:673:54889:12:11:71:529:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:especially prevalent in the 50-75th quartile – classes that are somewhat above average in terms of suspiciousness.  
27:674:55005:11:12:71:532:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:Thus, one might observe a spurious rise in the frequency of extreme values as one moves from classrooms that are 
27:675:55118:12:11:71:530:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:not all suspicious to those that are somewhat suspicious, simply because the fraction of undetected cheaters rises.  
27:676:55235:11:12:71:534:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:On the other hand, it may be the case that the degree of correlation between ANSWERS and SCORE may vary over 
27:677:55344:12:11:71:540:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:the distribution.  In particular, there may be a positive correlation between those two variables in the right-tail of the 
27:678:55467:11:12:71:486:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:distribution, even if teachers are not cheating.  This would lead us to overstate the number of cheaters.. 
27:679:55574:12:0:71:74:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!: 
28:680:55576:12:27:107:538:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The bottom panel of Table 3 reverses the exercise, showing how the likelihood of having 
28:681:55664:27:28:71:538:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:suspicious answer strings changes as one moves from low quartiles of SCORE to high quartiles.  
28:682:55759:28:27:71:511:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Note that the patterns are reversed.  Classes that are in the bottom quartile on SCORE have 
28:683:55851:27:28:71:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:relatively high rates of suspicious strings. The probabilities of suspicious strings for classes in 
28:684:55951:28:28:71:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the second and third quartile are nearly identical to one another, and much lower than those of 
28:685:56047:28:27:71:160:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the first quartile.   
28:686:56069:27:28:107:535:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The key question here is the frequency with which one would observe extreme values of 
28:687:56155:28:27:71:523:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:one of the cheating measures when the other cheating measure is also an outlier, assuming no 
28:688:56248:27:28:71:537:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating occurred.  One can imagine a variety of sensible approaches to predicting the upper tail 
28:689:56346:28:27:71:528:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:using the information in Table 3.  For example, one could fit a linear or quadratic model to the 
28:690:56443:27:28:71:507:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:patterns observed in the lower portion of the distribution and extrapolate the estimates.  In 
28:691:56537:28:28:71:512:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:practice, however, the trends in the 0-75th percentile of the distribution are so weak that the 
28:692:56633:28:27:71:531:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:results we obtain are not sensitive to the precise formulation.  Consequently, we simply use the 
28:693:56730:27:28:71:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:values in the 50-75th percentile as our estimate of what would have happened in the upper tail, 
28:694:56826:28:27:71:160:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:absent cheating.    
28:695:56846:27:28:71:74:295:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:!: 
28:696:56846:55:28:71:272:267:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:c) Estimating the Prevalence of Cheating 
28:697:56887:28:27:107:505:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Our key equation for estimating the frequency of cheating, presented earlier in the 
28:698:56971:27:31:71:173:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:modeling section, is  
28:699:56993:31:0:71:250:181:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:(1) )(ˆncnchucheatASNNN××−= 
29:700:57022:0:27:71:542:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:which simply says that the estimated number of cheating classes is equal to the number of classes 
29:701:57120:27:28:71:539:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that are outliers on both the cheating measures, minus the number of classes we would expect by 
29:702:57216:28:30:71:523:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:chance to be high on both measures based on the distribution of the measures in non-cheating 
29:703:57309:30:28:71:525:623:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms.  Guided by the results presented above, we compute ncS as the fraction of classes 
29:704:57403:28:31:71:542:595:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with SCORE above a certain threshold, conditional on being in the 50-75th percentile on answers, 
29:705:57500:31:27:71:186:564:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and vice-versa for ncA. 
29:706:57524:27:28:107:534:537:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: The top panel of Table 4 presents our estimates of the percentage of classrooms that are 
29:707:57614:28:28:71:535:509:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating on average on a given subject test (i.e. reading comprehension or one of the three math 
29:708:57711:28:27:71:538:481:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tests) in a given year.  We present a 3 x 3 matrix of estimates corresponding to how stringent the 
29:709:57810:27:28:71:505:454:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:thresholds are for judging whether a classroom’s test score fluctuations and answer string 
29:710:57901:28:27:71:532:426:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:patterns qualify as suspicious.  The estimated prevalence of cheaters ranges from 1.1 percent to 
29:711:57998:27:28:71:532:399:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:2.1 percent, depending on the particular set of cutoffs used.  As would be expected, the number 
29:712:58094:28:28:71:492:371:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of cheaters is generally declining as higher thresholds are employed.  Nonetheless, it is 
29:713:58184:28:27:71:516:343:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:encouraging that over such a wide range of cutoffs, the range of estimates is relatively tight. 
29:714:58280:27:28:107:531:316:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The bottom panel of Table 4 presents estimates of the percentage of classrooms that are 
29:715:58368:28:27:71:536:288:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating on any of the four subject tests in a particular year.  If every classroom that cheated did 
29:716:58469:27:28:71:529:261:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:so only on one subject test, than the results in the bottom panel would simply be four times the 
29:717:58566:28:28:71:519:233:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:results in the top panel.  In many instances, however, classrooms appear to cheat on multiple 
29:718:58660:28:62:71:474:205:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subjects.  Thus, the prevalence rates range from 3.4-5.6 percent of all classrooms.22 
29:719:58745:62:7:215:218:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
29:720:58803:69:16:71:521:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:22  Computation of the overall prevalence is relatively complicated because it involves calculating not only how 
29:721:58916:16:12:71:521:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:many classrooms are actually above the thresholds on multiple subject tests, but also how frequently this would 
29:722:59028:12:0:71:519:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:occur in the absence of cheating.  The full programming solution to this problem is available from the authors.  
30:723:59143:0:27:107:501:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Table 5 presents breakdowns of cheating by grade and subject.  Rows in the table 
30:724:59224:27:28:71:532:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:correspond to grades and columns represent different subject tests.  Several interesting findings 
30:725:59322:28:27:71:534:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:stand out.  The third grade has the highest cheating rates, which is likely due to the fact that this 
30:726:59424:27:28:71:506:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:grade is the only one in which teachers are permitted to administer the exams to their own 
30:727:59515:28:28:71:532:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students.  Cheating rates also tend to be higher in sixth grade, which may be due to the fact that 
30:728:59614:28:27:71:490:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:this grade has traditionally been a focus of greater attention on the part of teachers and 
30:729:59705:27:28:71:534:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:administrators because statewide achievement exams are also administered in this grade.  If one 
30:730:59801:28:27:71:528:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:looks at specific subject tests, cheating rates are slightly higher on reading comprehension and 
30:731:59898:27:28:71:527:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the first and third math exams, while noticeably lower on the second math exam.  This may be 
30:732:59991:28:27:71:504:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:because the second math exam is located in the middle of the answer key, making it more 
30:733:60079:27:28:71:503:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:difficult to quickly change student answers.   In addition, in the upper grades, this section 
30:734:60173:28:28:71:519:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consists largely of questions that ask students to interpret graphs, charts and tables, and most 
30:735:60270:28:27:71:541:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students do relatively well on this section, so it is possible that teachers do not feel that they need 
30:736:60374:27:28:71:268:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to artificially inflate scores in this area.   
30:737:60421:28:28:107:110:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: 
30:738:60421:56:27:71:276:294:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:VI. Are We Really Detecting Cheating? 
30:739:60459:27:28:107:505:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:If accurate, the results above suggest cheating rates of 4-5 percent among Chicago 
30:740:60542:28:27:71:523:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:elementary school classrooms. Because of the necessarily indirect nature of our identification 
30:741:60637:27:28:71:518:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:strategy, a healthy skepticism towards our conclusions may be warranted. In this section, we 
30:742:60730:28:27:71:517:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:provide a range of supplemental analyses suggesting that the results are indeed cheating and 
30:743:60823:27:28:71:534:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:addressing possible competing explanations as to why the patterns we observe may have arisen. 
30:744:60917:28:0:107:110:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: 
31:745:60919:28:27:71:369:708:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:a)   Will our method find cheating, even if no cheating exists? 
31:746:60983:27:28:107:523:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Our identification relies on assumptions about how variables will be distributed in the 
31:747:61071:28:27:71:522:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tails of a distribution that is not directly observed.   It is conceivable that our assumptions are 
31:748:61171:27:28:71:508:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:inaccurate, falsely generating what appears to be evidence of cheating, even when no such 
31:749:61261:28:28:71:163:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating occurred. 
31:750:61280:28:27:89:519:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:  As a test of this possibility, we randomly assigned students to hypothetical classrooms.  
31:751:61372:27:28:71:496:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:These synthetic classrooms thus consisted of groups of students who in actuality had no 
31:752:61460:28:27:71:514:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:connection to one another.  We then analyzed these hypothetical classrooms using the same 
31:753:61550:27:28:71:531:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:algorithm applied to the actual data.  As one would hope, no evidence of cheating was found in 
31:754:61645:28:27:71:532:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the simulated classes.  Indeed, the estimated prevalence of cheating was slightly negatve in this 
31:755:61743:27:28:71:518:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:simulation, i.e. classrooms with large test score increases in the current year followed by big 
31:756:61839:28:28:71:536:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:declines the next year were slightly less likely to have unusual patterns of answer strings.  Thus, 
31:757:61939:28:27:71:534:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:we conclude that there is no evidence that our identification approach finds cheating even when 
31:758:62035:27:28:71:223:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:no cheating is actually present. 
31:759:62068:28:27:89:95:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:  
31:760:62070:55:28:71:535:295:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:b) Are classrooms with suspicious answer strings less likely to maintain large test score gains?  
31:761:62168:28:28:107:509:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Test score gains due to cheating should be completely transitory, assuming that the 
31:762:62252:28:27:71:535:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:likelihood of having a cheating teacher next year is the same for students who do or do not have 
31:763:62349:27:28:71:518:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:a cheating teacher this year.  In contrast, while there might be substantial mean reversion for 
31:764:62445:28:27:71:512:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms with large test score gains for reasons other than cheating, there might also be a 
31:765:62539:27:0:71:250:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:permanent component to such gains. 
32:766:62576:0:27:107:524:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:In conducting such a hypothesis test, we cannot, of course, use information about next 
32:767:62663:27:28:71:523:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:year’s test score as a basis for labeling a classroom a likely cheater (as we generally do in our 
32:768:62761:28:27:71:535:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating classification, see equation (2)).  We can, however, compare classrooms with large test 
32:769:62858:27:28:71:542:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:score gains this year that either do or do not have suspicious patterns of answer strings. The more 
32:770:62958:28:28:71:517:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:suspicious the answer strings, the more likely is cheating, and the greater the expected mean 
32:771:63052:28:27:71:287:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:reversion in the following year’s test scores. 
32:772:63099:27:28:107:513:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:  Table 6 presents the results of this analysis.  The top panel of the table restricts the 
32:773:63190:28:27:71:541:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sample to the ten percent of classrooms with the greatest test score gains in reading in the current 
32:774:63291:27:28:71:536:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:year, relative to other classes in that grade and year.  The middle panel and bottom panel look at 
32:775:63390:28:27:71:531:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the top 5 percent and top 1 percent respectively of classroom test score gains.23 Reported in the 
32:776:63488:27:28:71:536:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:table are the mean excess gain in these classes in the base year (i.e., the gains above and beyond 
32:777:63587:28:28:71:531:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the mean gain for all classrooms in the system on a given subject, grade, and test that year), the 
32:778:63686:28:27:71:541:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:excess gain for the same students the following year, and the percent of the base year excess gain 
32:779:63785:27:28:71:529:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that is maintained.  Columns in the table correspond to how suspicious the classroom’s answer 
32:780:63879:28:27:71:529:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:string patterns were: below the 50th percentile, 50th-80th percentile, 80th-95th percentile, 95th-
32:781:63977:27:28:71:512:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:99th, and greater than the 99th percentile.  We expect the fraction of cheating classrooms to 
32:782:64071:28:28:71:541:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase as the answer strings become more suspicious.  Consequently, the fraction of the current 
32:783:64169:28:27:71:542:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:year’s excess test score gain relative to the mean classroom in that subject, grade, and year that is 
32:784:64271:27:28:71:480:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:maintained the following year should decrease moving from left to right in the table. 
32:785:64357:28:27:107:506:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Looking first at the top panel of Table 6, among the ten percent of classes with the 
32:786:64442:27:26:71:517:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:greatest test score gains, those whose answer strings are not at all suspicious (below the 50th 
32:787:64537:26:7:215:218:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
32:788:64595:33:0:71:519:124:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:23 Reiterating what was written above, it cannot be emphasized enough that this table differs from our previous 
33:789:64709:0:27:71:542:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percentile on ANSWERS) gain on average .59 grade equivalents more than the system-wide mean 
33:790:64801:27:28:71:510:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in the base year.  Students in these classrooms do perform slightly worse than expected the 
33:791:64893:28:27:71:534:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:following year (-.11 grade equivalents).  Nonetheless, at the end of the next year, these students 
33:792:64992:27:28:71:485:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:maintain 81 percent of the base year excess gain through the following year (i.e., (.59-
33:793:65080:28:28:71:536:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:.11)/.59=.81).  As one moves from left to right in the table towards classrooms more likely to be 
33:794:65178:28:27:71:518:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating, an increasing fraction of the current year’s gains are lost, as predicted.  In the most
