33:796:65370:28:27:71:523:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent of the apparent gains in the current year evaporate in the next year’s test.24  Note also 
33:797:65468:27:28:71:530:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that classes with suspicious answer strings are greatly over-represented among those achieving 
33:798:65563:28:27:71:514:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:large test score gains, consistent with the prediction that our two cheating indicators will be 
33:799:65659:27:28:71:288:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:highly positively correlated in the upper tail. 
33:800:65707:28:28:107:513:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:One possible concern that arises from the top panel of the table is whether the mean 
33:801:65792:28:27:71:519:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:reversion is greater on the right-hand-side columns of the table simply because the base-year 
33:802:65886:27:28:71:531:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:gains are larger.  The bottom two panels of Table 6 demonstrate that this is not the case.  When 
33:803:65983:28:27:71:541:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the sample is restricted to classrooms whose test score gains are in the top five percent or top one 
33:804:66084:27:28:71:512:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent of all classes, very similar patterns appear.  Classrooms that do not have suspicious 
33:805:66178:28:28:71:530:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:answer strings continue to exhibit little mean reversion, even though the base year gains in this 
33:806:66276:28:27:71:518:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subset are even greater than the base year gains in the far right column of the top panel.  The 
33:807:66372:27:58:71:509:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more suspicious the answer strings, the greater the mean reversion.  Thus, these results are 
33:808:66465:58:11:539:542:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                                                                                                                                                           
33:809:66651:69:12:71:522:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:analysis in that we are in no way conditioning on the following year’s test scores, unlike when we construct our 
33:810:66764:12:7:71:150:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:cheating estimates. 
33:811:66784:7:16:71:504:124:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:24  We do not expect the test score gains to completely disappear because even among the classes with very 
33:812:66891:16:0:71:332:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:suspicious answer strings, not all of the classrooms are cheating. 
34:813:66960:0:27:71:522:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consistent with the hypothesis that cheating is the explanation for the large number of classes 
34:814:67056:27:28:71:372:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with both suspicious answer strings and large test score gains. 
34:815:67120:28:27:107:110:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: 
34:816:67120:55:28:71:375:626:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:c) Do the same teachers and schools tend to cheat repeatedly? 
34:817:67182:28:28:107:512:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:If what we are detecting is truly cheating, then one would expect that a teacher who 
34:818:67267:28:27:71:520:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheats on one part of the test would be more likely to cheat on other parts of the test.  Also, a 
34:819:67365:27:28:71:523:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:teacher who cheats one year would be more likely to cheat the following year.  Finally, to the 
34:820:67460:28:27:71:540:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:extent that cheating is either condoned by the principal or carried out by the test coordinator, one 
34:821:67561:27:28:71:527:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:would expect to find multiple classes in a school cheating in any given year, and perhaps even 
34:822:67656:28:27:71:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that cheating in a school one year predicts cheating in future years. If what we are detecting is 
34:823:67754:27:28:71:521:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:not cheating, then one would not necessarily expect to find strong correlation in our cheating 
34:824:67849:28:28:71:490:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:indicators across exams for a specific classroom, across classrooms, or across years.25  
34:825:67938:28:27:107:536:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Table 7 reports regression results testing these predictions.  The dependent variable is an 
34:826:68030:27:28:71:531:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:indicator for whether we believe a classroom is likely to be cheating on a particular subject test 
34:827:68129:28:27:71:534:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:using our most stringent definition (above the 95th percentile on both cheating indicators).   The 
34:828:68228:27:28:71:530:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:baseline probability of qualifying as a cheater for this cutoff is 1.1 percent.  To fully appreciate 
34:829:68329:28:28:71:531:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the enormity of the effects implied by the table, it is important to keep this very low baseline in 
34:830:68429:28:27:71:503:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:mind.  We report estimates from linear probability models (probits yield similar marginal 
34:831:68519:27:46:71:355:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:effects), with standard errors clustered at the school level.  
34:832:68582:46:7:215:218:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
34:833:68640:53:16:71:519:159:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:25 Alternatively, if one thought that cheating were an individual teacher phenomenon, but school improvement, 
34:834:68750:16:12:71:519:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:instructional quality or curricular content were a school-wide phenomena, then one might construe correlations 
34:835:68861:12:11:71:528:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:within schools and over time as evidence against cheating.  Given the fact that most teachers do not monitor their 
34:836:68976:11:12:71:540:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:own exams, and that the test coordinator plays such a large role in the testing process within each school, we tend to 
34:837:69095:12:0:71:220:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:think this scenario is less plausible.   
35:838:69138:0:27:107:533:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Column 1 of Table 7 shows that cheating on other tests in the same year is an extremely 
35:839:69226:27:28:71:534:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:powerful predictor of cheating in a different subject.  If a classroom cheats on exactly one other 
35:840:69325:28:27:71:523:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subject test, the predicted probability of cheating on this test increases by over ten percentage 
35:841:69423:27:28:71:523:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:points.  Since the baseline cheating rates are only 1.1 percent, classrooms cheating on exactly 
35:842:69519:28:28:71:530:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:one other test are ten times more likely to have cheated on this subject than are classrooms that 
35:843:69617:28:27:71:539:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:did not cheat on any of the other subjects (which is the omitted category).  Classrooms that cheat 
35:844:69716:27:28:71:528:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:on two other subjects are almost 30 times more likely to cheat on this test, relative to those not 
35:845:69815:28:27:71:531:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating on other tests.  If a class cheats on all three other subjects, it is 50 times more likely to 
35:846:69918:27:28:71:180:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:also cheat on this test. 
35:847:69943:28:27:107:533:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:There also is evidence of correlation in cheating within schools.  A ten percentage-point 
35:848:70033:27:28:71:525:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase in cheating classrooms in a school (excluding the classroom in question) on the same 
35:849:70127:28:28:71:505:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subject test raises the likelihood this class cheats by roughly .016 percentage points.  This 
35:850:70221:28:27:71:537:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:potentially suggests some role for centralized cheating by a school counselor, test coordinator or 
35:851:70320:27:28:71:509:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the principal, rather than by teachers operating independently.  There is little evidence that 
35:852:70415:28:27:71:473:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating rates within the school on other subject tests affects cheating on this test.   
35:853:70504:27:28:107:540:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:When making comparisons across years (columns 3 and 4), it is important to note that we 
35:854:70592:28:28:71:516:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:do not actually have teacher identifiers.  We do, however, know what classroom a student is 
35:855:70684:28:27:71:529:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:assigned to.  Thus, we can only compare the correlation between past and current cheating in a 
35:856:70779:27:28:71:533:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:given classroom.  To the extent that teacher turnover occurs or teachers switch classrooms, this 
35:857:70876:28:27:71:537:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:proxy will be contaminated by serious measurement error.  Even given this important limitation, 
35:858:70972:27:28:71:538:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating in the classroom last year predicts cheating this year.  In column 3, for example, we see 
35:859:71071:28:0:71:532:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that classroom’s that cheated in the same subject last year are 9.6 percentage points more likely 
36:860:71171:0:27:71:510:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to cheat this year, even after we control for cheating on other subjects in the same year and 
36:861:71265:27:28:71:501:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating in other classes in the school.  Column 4 shows that prior cheating in the school 
36:862:71356:28:27:71:408:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:strongly predicts the likelihood that a classroom will cheat this year.   
36:863:71430:27:28:107:110:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: 
36:864:71430:55:28:71:472:598:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:d) Is it really student cheating rather than teacher cheating that we are detecting?  
36:865:71516:28:27:107:495:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Although our explanation focuses on teachers, it is also conceivable that there is 
36:866:71599:27:28:71:520:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:something unusual about students in classes that we label as cheating (e.g., a particular set of 
36:867:71696:28:27:71:516:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:student skills, high effort at the beginning of the test but not at the end, students copying off 
36:868:71794:27:28:71:524:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:other student exams) that might lead to suspicious answer strings.  If that is the case, then one 
36:869:71892:28:27:71:538:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:would predict that the same students who have suspicious answer strings one year would also be 
36:870:71987:27:28:71:542:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:likely to have suspicious answer strings the next year – much as we observed above that cheating 
36:871:72084:28:28:71:539:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in a classroom one year predicts cheating in a classroom the next year. We test this hypothesis in 
36:872:72183:28:27:71:527:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:two ways.  First, for each student in a given subject and year, we compute how unlikely it was 
36:873:72278:27:28:71:529:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:for the most unusual block of answers that student was part of to occur (this corresponds to the 
36:874:72375:28:27:71:510:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:first of the suspicious string measures we introduced in Section III).  We then calculate the 
36:875:72469:27:28:71:488:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:student-level correlation from one year to the next on that measure.  The correlation is 
36:876:72558:28:28:71:521:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:approximately .01, suggesting that students who are part of suspicious blocks of answers one 
36:877:72651:28:27:71:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:year are not especially likely to be part of suspicious blocks the following year.  Similarly, we 
36:878:72749:27:28:71:472:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compare the same student across years to determine whether some students tend to 
36:879:72830:28:27:71:522:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:systematically get hard questions correct and easy questions wrong (the last of the suspicious 
36:880:72925:27:28:71:502:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:string measures we introduced).  The year-to-year correlation in that measure is .07.  The 
36:881:73016:28:0:71:509:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:absence in persistence in suspicious answer patterns over time for a given student makes it 
37:882:73110:0:27:71:506:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:unlikely that our results are being driven by student cheating, since one would expect that 
37:883:73202:27:28:71:537:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students who cheat one year would be likely to cheat with high probability the next year as well. 
37:884:73300:28:27:107:110:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: 
37:885:73300:55:28:71:418:626:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:C:e) Are we mistaking emphasis on certain subject material for cheating? 
37:886:73371:28:28:107:527:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:If a math teacher spends several months on fractions with a particular class, one would 
37:887:73459:28:27:71:513:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:expect the class to do particularly well on all of the math questions relating to fractions and 
37:888:73555:27:28:71:531:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:perhaps worse than average on other math questions.26  Such patterns might wrongly lead us to 
37:889:73649:28:27:71:353:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:deem a classroom’s answer strings to be suspicious.27        
37:890:73710:27:28:107:499:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Table 8 shows OLS estimates of the relationship between whether a classroom is 
37:891:73789:28:27:71:542:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:categorized as a cheater and the nature of the across-question correlations in the classroom on the 
37:892:73889:27:28:71:541:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:first math exam.  Seven different math skills/areas are tested in this exam: numeration, geometry, 
37:893:73988:28:28:71:522:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:measurement, fractions, algebra, statistics and estimation.  The dependent variable in the first 
37:894:74085:28:27:71:513:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and third columns is the number of different item-types for the three and five questions in a 
37:895:74179:27:28:71:531:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:particular classroom that are most suspicious.  The dependent variable in the second and fourth 
37:896:74275:28:27:71:537:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:columns is a binary indicator of whether the three (five) most suspicious questions all fell in one 
37:897:74375:27:28:71:539:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:area.  Note first that the mean values, reported in brackets, show that there is generally very little 
37:898:74478:28:44:71:543:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:concentration in the types of questions that are most suspicious within a classroom.  For instance, 
37:899:74578:44:7:215:218:223:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
37:900:74636:51:16:71:524:216:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:26 One might imagine a similar scenario on the reading exam. If a teacher spends an entire semester studying the 
37:901:74749:16:11:71:529:200:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:Underground Railroad, and the reading exam that year happens to include a passage on this topic, it would not be 
37:902:74862:11:12:71:536:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:surprising to find that an extremely high number of students in the class correctly answer all of the items relating to 
37:903:74982:12:11:71:533:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:this passage, which may appear as a highly suspicious answer string.  However, it is also likely that when teachers 
37:904:75098:11:12:71:530:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:cheat on the reading comprehension exam, they focus on a specific passage since each passage and the associated 
37:905:75210:12:11:71:539:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:questions are generally on the same page.  Thus, on the reading exam, it is difficult to distinguish between instances 
37:906:75329:11:7:71:320:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:of cheating and honest passage knowledge by the students.     
37:907:75391:7:16:71:535:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:27 Although there is no reason for such classrooms to have elevated test score gains or especially large losses in the 
37:908:75510:16:12:71:536:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:following year, which reduces concern that teacher emphasis on specific subject material will lead us to exaggerate 
37:909:75626:12:0:71:173:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:the degree of cheating.    
38:910:75655:0:27:71:537:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in the typical classroom the three most suspicious questions were spread over 2.4 different types 
38:911:75753:27:28:71:538:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of items, and in only 7.7 percent of classrooms did all three questions fall within the same type.   
38:912:75854:28:27:107:542:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The coefficient estimates in Table 8 suggest that the patterns in classrooms categorized as 
38:913:75946:27:28:71:481:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheaters were only slightly different than in other classrooms.  Focusing on the basic 
38:914:76033:28:28:71:536:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:specification in the top row of the table, the point estimates in columns (1) and (3) are small and 
38:915:76133:28:27:71:524:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:statistically insignificant.  The coefficient in column (4) is significantly higher in the cheating 
38:916:76233:27:28:71:541:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms.  That result, however, appears to be an artifact of the particular classification of item 
38:917:76335:28:27:71:538:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:types.  When one uses a more disaggregated classification scheme (the second row), or excludes 
38:918:76430:27:28:71:522:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the very broad category of numeration (the third row), any evidence that cheating classrooms 
38:919:76523:28:27:71:520:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tend to have more concentration in their suspicious answers disappears. These results are not 
38:920:76617:27:28:71:425:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sensitive to the inclusion of a variety of classroom and school covariates. 
38:921:76693:28:28:107:110:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: 
38:922:76693:56:27:71:339:377:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:VII. Does Teacher Cheating Respond to Incentives? 
38:923:76743:27:28:107:512:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:From the perspective of economics, perhaps the most interesting question related to 
38:924:76827:28:27:71:538:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:teacher cheating is the degree to which it is sensitive to incentives.  As noted in the introduction, 
38:925:76929:27:28:71:529:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:there were two major changes in the incentives faced by teachers and students over our sample 
38:926:77023:28:28:71:527:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:period.  Prior to 1996, ITBS scores were primarily used to provide teachers and parents with a 
38:927:77118:28:27:71:536:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sense of how a child was progressing academically.  Beginning in 1996 with the appointment of 
38:928:77212:27:28:71:520:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Paul Vallas as CEO of Schools, the CPS launched an initiative designed to hold students and 
38:929:77304:28:0:71:280:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:teachers accountable for student learning.   
39:930:77351:0:27:107:532:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The reform had two main elements.  The first was putting schools “on probation” if less 
39:931:77439:27:28:71:518:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:than 15 percent of students scored at or above national norms on the ITBS reading exams.28  
39:932:77531:28:27:71:531:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Probation schools that do not exhibit sufficient improvement may be reconstituted, a procedure 
39:933:77626:27:28:71:538:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that involves closing the school and dismissing or reassigning all of the school staff.29  It is clear 
39:934:77729:28:28:71:524:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:from our discussions with teachers and administrators that being on probation is viewed as an 
39:935:77823:28:27:71:533:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:extremely undesirable circumstance.  The second piece of the accountability reform was an end 
39:936:77917:27:28:71:503:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to social promotion – the practice of passing students to the next grade regardless of their 
39:937:78010:28:27:71:538:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:academic skills or school performance.  Under the new policy, students in third, sixth and eighth 
39:938:78108:27:28:71:540:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:grade must meet minimum standards on the ITBS in both reading and mathematics in order to be 
39:939:78201:28:27:71:516:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:promoted to the next grade.  The promotion standards were implemented in Spring 1996 for 
39:940:78290:27:28:71:524:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:eighth grade students and in Spring 1997 for third and sixth graders.  Promotion decisions are 
39:941:78385:28:28:71:404:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f4:B:based solely on scores in reading comprehension and mathematics.30 
39:942:78451:28:27:107:542:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Table 9 presents OLS estimates of the relationship between teacher cheating and a variety 
39:943:78541:27:28:71:412:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of classroom and school characteristics.31  The unit of observation is a 
39:944:78614:28:27:71:540:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classroom*subject*grade*year.  The dependent variable is an indicator of whether the classroom 
39:945:78709:27:37:71:504:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheated.  Here we define cheating using our 95th percentile cutoff—that is, a classroom is 
39:946:78800:37:7:215:218:258:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
39:947:78858:44:12:71:360:251:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:28The CPS did not use math performance to determine probation status. 
39:948:78928:12:16:71:542:239:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:29  Seven high schools have been reconstituted to date, although no elementary schools have suffered this fate.  For a 
39:949:79047:16:7:71:466:223:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:more detailed analysis of the probation policy, see Jacob (2001) and Jacob and Lefgren (2001b).   
39:950:79145:7:16:71:516:216:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:30 In 1997, the promotion standards for third, sixth and eighth grade were 2.8, 5.3, and 7.0 respectively, which 
39:951:79258:16:11:71:535:200:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:roughly corresponded to the 20th percentile in the national achievement distribution.  Students who do not meet the 
39:952:79374:11:12:71:517:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:standard in June are required to attend a six-week summer school program, after which they retake the exams.  
39:953:79484:12:11:71:518:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:Those students who pass the August exams move on to the next grade.  Students who again fail are required to 
39:954:79593:11:12:71:541:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:repeat the grade, with the exception of 15-year-olds who attend newly created “transition” centers.  In 1997, roughly 
39:955:79711:12:11:71:540:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:30-40 percent of the students in these grades attended summer school and 20 percent of third graders and 12 percent 
39:956:79827:11:12:71:525:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:of sixth and eighth graders were retained.  For a more detailed analysis of the social promotion policy, see Jacob 
39:957:79942:12:7:71:231:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:(2001) and Jacob and Lefgren (2001a). 
39:958:79980:7:16:71:538:124:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:31 Logit models evaluated at the mean yield comparable results, so the estimates from a linear probability model are 
39:959:80097:16:0:71:219:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:presented for ease of interpretation.  
40:960:80138:0:27:71:524:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:designated a cheater if its SCORE and ANSWERS are above the 95th percentile in that grade, 
40:961:80229:27:28:71:514:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:subject and year.32  In column 1, the policy changes are restricted to have a constant impact 
40:962:80323:28:27:71:504:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:across all classrooms.  We see that the introduction of the social promotion and probation 
40:963:80414:27:28:71:520:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:policies is positively correlated with the likelihood of classroom cheating, although the point 
40:964:80510:28:28:71:534:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimates are not statistically significant at conventional levels.  However, cheating does appear 
40:965:80609:28:27:71:523:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to be responsive to other costs and benefits.  Classrooms that tested poorly last year are much 
40:966:80705:27:28:71:515:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more likely to cheat.  For example, a classroom with average student prior achievement one 
40:967:80796:28:27:71:521:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classroom standard deviation below the mean is 23 percent more likely to cheat.  Classrooms 
40:968:80888:27:28:71:518:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with students in multiple grades are 65 percent less likely to cheat than classrooms where all 
40:969:80983:28:27:71:532:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students are in the same grade.  This is consistent with the fact that it is likely more difficult for 
40:970:81086:27:28:71:511:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:teachers in such classrooms to cheat, since they must administer two different test forms to 
40:971:81179:28:28:71:540:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students, which will necessarily have different correct answers.   Moreover, classes with a higher 
40:972:81278:28:27:71:535:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:proportion of students who are included in the official test reporting are more likely to cheat—a 
40:973:81376:27:28:71:536:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:10 percentage point increase in the proportion of students in a class who test scores “count” will 
40:974:81475:28:27:71:537:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increase the likelihood of cheating by roughly 20 percent.  Teachers who administer the exam to 
40:975:81571:27:28:71:540:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:their own students are 0.67 percentage points—approximately 50 percent—more likely to cheat.  
40:976:81665:28:28:71:541:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, there is no statistically significant impact on cheating of reusing a test form that has been 
40:977:81768:28:27:71:514:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:administered in a previous year.  That finding is of interest because it suggests that teachers 
40:978:81864:27:28:71:541:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:taking old exams and teaching the precise questions to students is not an important component of 
40:979:81961:28:41:71:522:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:what we are detecting as cheating (although anecdotal evidence suggests this practice exists). 
40:980:82056:41:7:215:218:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
40:981:82114:48:16:71:523:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:32 The results are not sensitive to the cheating cutoff used.  Note that this measure may include error due to both 
40:982:82230:16:12:71:533:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:false positives and negatives.  Since the measurement error is in the dependent variable, it will simply decrease the 
40:983:82348:12:0:71:182:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:precision of our estimates.  
41:984:82379:0:27:107:512:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Much more interesting results emerge when we interact the policy changes with the 
41:985:82461:27:28:71:537:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:previous year’s test scores for the classroom.  For both probation and social promotion, cheating 
41:986:82559:28:27:71:541:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rates in the lowest performing classrooms prove to be quite sensitive to the change in incentives.  
41:987:82659:27:28:71:516:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:In column 2, a classroom one-standard deviation below the mean increases cheating by 0.43 
41:988:82749:28:28:71:535:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percentage points in response to the school probation policy and roughly 0.65 percentage points 
41:989:82845:28:27:71:517:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:due to the ending of social promotion.  Given the baseline cheating rate of 1.1 percent, these 
41:990:82940:27:28:71:540:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:effects are substantial.  The magnitude of these changes are particularly large considering that no 
41:991:83040:28:27:71:534:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:elementary school on probation has ever been reconstituted since this policy was put into place, 
41:992:83137:27:28:71:479:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and that the social promotion policy has a direct impact on students, but not obvious 
41:993:83223:28:27:71:534:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:ramifications for teacher pay or rewards.33  A classroom one standard deviation above the mean 
41:994:83318:27:28:71:528:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:does not see any significant change in cheating in response to these two policies.  Such classes 
41:995:83415:28:28:71:540:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:are very unlikely to be located in schools at risk for being put on probation, and also are likely to 
41:996:83517:28:27:71:523:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have few students at risk for being retained.   The specification shown in column 3 includes a 
41:997:83612:27:28:71:532:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:number of classroom and school characteristics, which do not appear to change the coefficients 
41:998:83707:28:27:71:523:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:on the policy variables.   Consistent with the prior achievement results, classrooms in schools 
41:999:83803:27:28:71:535:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with lower achievement, higher poverty rates and more Black students are more likely to cheat.  
41:1000:83899:28:67:71:522:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Interestingly, classrooms in schools with higher quality teachers are less likely to cheat while 
41:1001:83996:67:7:215:218:200:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
41:1002:84054:74:16:71:540:193:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:33 While this trend is particularly disturbing due to the relatively minor incentives, given the relatively small number 
41:1003:84175:16:11:71:529:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:of classrooms engaged in cheating, it is unlikely that such explicit test manipulation has had a large impact on the 
41:1004:84292:11:12:71:517:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:average achievement levels in Chicago, or the observed increase in achievement since the introduction of high-
41:1005:84402:12:11:71:518:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:stakes testing.  Table 8 suggests that the accountability policies increased the likelihood of cheating in any one 
41:1006:84517:11:12:71:540:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:subject by roughly 0.5 to 1.0 percentage points (depending on whether the effects of social promotion and probation 
41:1007:84633:12:11:71:540:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:are additive and which grade/subject one considers).  Now suppose that a teacher manipulates the reading exams for 
41:1008:84748:11:12:71:528:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:his or her students in a manner that artificially raises their test scores by 2 grade equivalent (which is much larger 
41:1009:84867:12:0:71:553:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:than we actually observe in the data).  This would inflate the system-wide average reading levels by only 0.01 GEs.       
42:1010:84991:0:27:71:532:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms in schools with younger teachers are more likely to cheat.  Column 4 illustrates that 
42:1011:85088:27:28:71:483:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the effects on the policy variables are robust to including school*year fixed effects.34 
42:1012:85176:28:27:107:541:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:It is also interesting to examine for which students teachers change answers when they do 
42:1013:85266:27:28:71:535:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheat.  One might imagine that teachers would cheat for lower-achieving students, or those who 
42:1014:85361:28:28:71:537:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the teacher believed could or should have done better on the exam.  However, it is not clear how 
42:1015:85458:28:27:71:524:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:precisely teachers are able to target their cheating behavior.  It is likely that time pressure and 
42:1016:85558:27:28:71:538:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:concerns about detection will limit the time teachers spend on cheating, and a brief inspection of 
42:1017:85657:28:27:71:484:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:an answer key will only provide a rough idea of how the student would score without 
42:1018:85741:27:28:71:515:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:manipulation of his or her answers.  Table 10 presents estimates of the relationship between 
42:1019:85834:28:27:71:536:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:observable student characteristics and cheating.  The unit of analysis is a student and the sample 
42:1020:85933:27:28:71:534:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is restricted to students in classrooms that were categorized as cheating using the 95th percentile 
42:1021:86033:28:28:71:538:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cutoff.  The dependent variable takes on the value of one if an individual student’s answer string 
42:1022:86132:28:27:71:533:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and test score pattern was suspicious at the 95th percentile level, suggesting that the teacher had 
42:1023:86232:27:28:71:520:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheated for that student in the particular subject and year.  The results are not sensitive to the 
42:1024:86331:28:27:71:499:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:particular cutoffs used.  The first two columns include all cheating schools; the final two 
42:1025:86423:27:28:71:493:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:columns narrow the sample to low-achieving schools, where the cheating appears to be 
42:1026:86508:28:28:71:508:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:concentrated.  All of the specifications include fixed effects for classroom*year so that the 
42:1027:86602:28:27:71:540:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:coefficients are estimated off of variation across students within a particular classroom.  Because 
42:1028:86702:27:46:71:523:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:a student’s test score at t-1 is highly correlated with the cheating indicator (by definition), the 
42:1029:86802:46:7:215:218:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
42:1030:86860:53:16:71:510:159:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:34 Another possible incentive that teachers might respond to is the likelihood of punishment.  Punishment for 
42:1031:86970:16:12:71:509:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:cheating, however, is extremely rare, with only two known instances of cheating teachers being disciplined.  
42:1032:87079:12:11:71:522:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:Beginning in 1996, CPS began doing audits of test scores.  Initially, these were mostly random in nature.  More 
42:1033:87191:11:12:71:533:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:recently, they have focused on classrooms with large test score gains.  Our data on audits is incomplete, however.  
42:1034:87307:12:0:71:529:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:When we included information on audits in the regressions, no statistically significant coefficients were obtained. 
43:1035:87425:0:27:71:540:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:equations are estimated using 2SLS where a student’s test scores at t-2 are used to instrument for 
43:1036:87524:27:28:71:245:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f4:B:the student’s t-1 achievement level. 
43:1037:87560:28:27:107:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:In column 1, teachers are roughly 6 percentage points more likely to cheat for students 
43:1038:87648:27:28:71:514:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:who scored in the second quartile (between the 25th and 50th percentile) in the prior year, as 
43:1039:87743:28:28:71:535:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compared to students scoring at the third or fourth quartiles.  Interestingly, teachers appear least 
43:1040:87844:28:27:71:536:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:likely to cheat for the lowest-achieving students (the coefficient on the bottom quartile indicator 
43:1041:87944:27:28:71:506:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is negative although not statistically significant).  Teachers are also less likely to cheat for 
43:1042:88041:28:27:71:523:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:students who are excluded from test reporting, as would be expected. Teachers also appear to 
43:1043:88134:27:28:71:326:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:less frequently cheat for boys and for older students. 
43:1044:88189:28:27:107:509:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Column 2 presents an alternative specification that includes a linear measure of the 
43:1045:88274:27:28:71:501:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:student’s prior achievement along with the interaction between prior achievement and an 
43:1046:88362:28:28:71:499:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:indicator for the high-stakes testing regime (encompassing both the probation and social 
43:1047:88451:28:27:71:527:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:promotion policies). 35  Here we see that, prior to the introduction of the accountability policy, 
43:1048:88550:27:28:71:503:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:teachers were more likely to cheat for higher achieving students.  The shift by teachers to 
43:1049:88642:28:27:71:542:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cheating for lower-achieving students after accountability measures were introduced is consistent 
43:1050:88740:27:28:71:535:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with the change in incentives.  School probation is based on the fraction of students exceeding a 
43:1051:88838:28:28:71:536:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:minimum threshold of competence.  Student promotion requires a student meeting a hurdle well 
43:1052:88931:28:27:71:510:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:below the median student in the system.  Columns 3 and 4 demonstrate that the same basic 
43:1053:89020:27:28:71:364:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:relationships hold for the subset of lower-achieving schools. 
43:1054:89082:28:41:71:74:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: 
43:1055:89082:69:7:215:218:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:!:                                                           
43:1056:89140:76:16:71:530:136:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:35 Ideally, one would also like to include interactions between prior student achievement and the social promotion 
43:1057:89255:16:12:71:541:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:and school probation policies in specifications that parallel Column 1.  Unfortunately, the standard errors become so 
43:1058:89373:12:0:71:259:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:D:large that no useful conclusions can be drawn. 
44:1059:89422:0:27:71:163:708:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f3:C:VIII.  Conclusion 
44:1060:89439:27:28:107:531:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:This paper develops an algorithm for determining the prevalence of teacher cheating on 
44:1061:89526:28:27:71:537:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:standardized tests and applies the results to data from the Chicago Public Schools.  Our methods 
44:1062:89623:27:28:71:509:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:reveal over 1,000 separate instances of classroom cheating, representing 4-5 percent of the 
44:1063:89715:28:28:71:542:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:classrooms.  Moreover, we find that teacher cheating appears quite responsive to relatively minor 
44:1064:89813:28:27:71:180:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:changes in incentives. 
44:1065:89836:27:28:107:532:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Our results suggest that the implementation of test-based accountability in schools must 
44:1066:89925:28:27:71:492:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:be approached with caution.  If accountability policies create strong incentives without 
44:1067:90014:27:28:71:516:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:instituting safeguards against cheating, we would predict substantial increases in teacher (or 
44:1068:90109:28:27:71:487:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:administrator) cheating.  This will not only decrease the effectiveness of the reform in 
44:1069:90198:27:28:71:510:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:identifying struggling schools or highlighting effective pedagogical practices, but will also 
44:1070:90292:28:28:71:518:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:undermine public confidence in school reform.  As high-stakes testing becomes increasingly 
44:1071:90383:28:27:71:516:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:widespread, these concerns will grow.  Fortunately, there are several, relatively inexpensive 
44:1072:90477:27:28:71:541:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:ways in which schools systems might prevent cheating.  Districts could hire an outside agency to 
44:1073:90574:28:27:71:520:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:proctor the exams rather than having teachers administer the tests.  Similarly, teachers in one 
44:1074:90670:27:28:71:390:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:school might be required to administer exams at another school.    
44:1075:90737:28:28:107:514:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:More generally, this paper fits into a small but growing body of research focused on 
44:1076:90822:28:27:71:534:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:identifying corrupt or illicit behavior on the part of economic actors (e.g. Porter and Zona 1993, 
44:1077:90921:27:28:71:513:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Fisman 2000, Di Tella and Schargrodsky 2001, Duggan and Levitt, forthcoming).  Because 
44:1078:91008:28:27:71:504:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individuals engaged in such behavior actively attempt to cover their trails, the intellectual 
44:1079:91102:27:28:71:498:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:exercise associated with uncovering their misdeeds differs substantially from the typical 
44:1080:91192:28:0:71:534:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:economic application in which the researcher starts with a well defined measure of the outcome 
45:1081:91289:0:27:71:536:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:variable (e.g. earnings, economic growth, profits) and then attempts to uncover the determinants 
45:1082:91386:27:28:71:504:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of these outcomes.  In the case of corruption, there is typically no clear outcome variable, 
45:1083:91479:28:27:71:530:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:making it necessary for the researcher to employ non-standard approaches in generating such a 
45:1084:91573:27:28:71:505:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:measure.  We hope that the methods utilized in this paper provide some guidance to those 
45:1085:91662:28:0:71:303:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:seeking to identify corruption in other domains.

50:1170:97216:55:27:71:390:708:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:!:Appendix A: The Construction of Suspicious String Measures 
50:1171:97275:27:28:107:530:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:We rely on two different indicators of cheating: (1) unusually large test score gains that 
50:1172:97366:28:27:74:531:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:are not sustained on future exams and (2) unexpected response patterns among students within 
50:1173:97459:27:28:74:539:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:the same classroom.  We measure the likelihood of classroom response patterns in four different 
50:1174:97555:28:28:74:532:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:ways.  This appendix describes in greater detail how we construct each of the four measures of 
50:1175:97650:28:27:74:257:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:unexpected or suspicious responses.   
50:1176:97688:27:28:107:508:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:The first measure focuses on the most unlikely block of identical answers given on 
50:1177:97771:28:27:74:527:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:consecutive questions.  This is meant to pick up teachers who change a series of questions for 
50:1178:97866:27:28:74:512:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:some number of students in their classroom.  For example, a teacher may fill in the correct 
50:1179:97958:28:27:74:536:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:responses for the last six questions on the exam for ten low-achieving students in the class.  We 
50:1180:98056:27:28:74:521:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:calculate the probability that this block of answers would have occurred if student responses 
50:1181:98150:28:28:74:530:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:within a classroom were uncorrelated.  The more unlikely is the most unexpected block of test 
50:1182:98244:28:27:74:336:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:responses, the more likely it is that cheating occurred. 
50:1183:98301:27:28:107:527:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:Using past test scores, future test scores and background characteristics, we predict the 
50:1184:98391:28:27:74:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:likelihood that each student will give each answer on each question.  For each item, a student 
50:1185:98486:27:28:74:531:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:has four choices (A, B, C or D), only one of which is correct.  We estimate a multinomial logit 
50:1186:98582:28:28:74:524:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:for each item on the exam in order to predict how students will respond to each question. We 
50:1187:98675:28:27:74:532:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:estimate the following model for each item, using information from other students in that year, 
50:1188:98771:27:39:74:170:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:grade and subject.   
50:1189:98792:39:18:88:112:173:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:(1)

51:1208:98919:27:28:74:523:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:responses (J) is four, and and Xs is a vector that includes measures of prior and future student 
51:1209:99015:28:27:74:522:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:achievement in math and reading as well as demographic variables (such as race, gender and 
51:1210:99106:27:28:74:533:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:free lunch status) for student s.  Thus, a student’s predicted probability of choosing a particular 
51:1211:99206:28:28:74:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:response is identified by the likelihood of other students (in the same year, grade and subject) 
51:1212:99303:28:27:74:406:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:with similar background characteristics choosing that response.         
51:1213:99375:27:28:107:529:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!: Notice that by including future as well as prior test scores in the model we decrease the 
51:1214:99465:28:27:71:530:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:likelihood that students with unusually good teachers will be identified as cheaters, since these 
51:1215:99563:27:28:71:530:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:students will likely retain some of the knowledge learned in the base year and thus have higher 
51:1216:99659:28:27:71:499:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:future test scores.  Also note that by estimating the probability of selecting each possible 
51:1217:99752:27:28:71:537:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:response, rather than simply estimating the probability of choosing the correct response, we take 
51:1218:99850:28:28:71:515:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:advantage of any additional information that is provided by particular response patterns in a 
51:1219:99944:28:27:71:126:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:!:classroom.
